percent o f total lending (slightly over the 50 percent level originally foreseen inthe CAS).

4.54    The proposed loan complements analytical and operational work done by other
members of the World Bank Group. As part o f its Municipal Scorecard pilot project in the


                                                                 55

Latin American region, IFC will measure municipal-level regulations for 25 of Brazil's most
important cities - including Siio Paulo, Rio de Janeiro, Salvador, Brasilia, and Fortaleza. With
the Municipality o f Siio Paulo, IFC i s also supporting the reform of the city's business
registration process. Inits turn, FIAS has taken the lead on a similar work at the state-level.

G.       FiduciaryArrangementsand Disbursement

ForeignExchangeControlEnvironment

4.55       The IMF Safeguards Assessment of the Central Bank of Brazil done in October 2002
and updated in March 2004 concluded that Banco Central does not present widespread
vulnerabilities that could compromise the safeguarding of Fund resources. In particular its
audit i s conducted by an internationally recognized audit firm, while its internal audit function
contributes effectively to internal control systems. The responses given by the Central Bank to
IMFrecommendations indicate that they were either implemented or are inthe process of being
implemented. Therefore fiom a fiduciary point o f view, the control environment, procedures and
regulations governing the bank's operations are generally adequate.




                                                      56

Public Financial Management of Budget Resources

4.56      The World Bankfinalized in 2002 a CFAA for Brazil, that was discussed with the
Government and which has been used to draw key conclusions on the country PFM. Brazil
has well developed financial management (,among the most robust in the Latin America and the
Caribbean Region), thus ensuring that Bank lending i s done in the context o f acceptable
oversight arrangements. Notwithstanding some desirable improvements that could be made (and
which are being tackled within the scope o f the reforms launched to sustain the Government's
focus to improve and modernize public sector management), the Brazilian system o f public
financial management provides reliable information, and adequate systems do exist to manage
and track the receipt and use o f funds at national level and there i s a high level o f fiscal
transparency. In particular, improved budget formats and enhanced internal controls to support
managerial decisions and external oversight; a new institutional set up for the Government's
audit function; as well as the expansion o f SIAFI to increase its programmatic functionality are
all important developments which took place after the delivery o f the CFAA. Regarding audits,
federal accounts are audited by SFC (Secretaria Federal de Controle Interno da Controladoria-
Geral da Uniiio) and by TCU (Tribunal de Contas da Uniiio) and thus their annual audits suffice,
and no audits o f the dedicated deposit accounts are required. All these conditions would support
any DPL program. In light o f the adequate control framework assisting public finance
operations, the risk to both Bank and country own funds is low.

4.57      The World Bank prepared a Country Procurement Assessment Report (CPAR) which
was discussed and agreed upon with the Government in 2004. Inaddition, the Bank i s currently
carrying out studies to assess both the systemic quality and performance o f the Brazilian public
sector procurement system. Public sector procurement in the federal government and some o f the
states i s overall adequate and the fiduciary risk related to procurement is rated by the CPAR as
average. While there are several areas which should be further modernized, the regulatory
framework adequately supports a competitive and transparent public procurement environment
and has fostered sound practices. Among other areas requiring improvement, are the bidders'
access to review of agencies' procurement decisions (i.e., bid protests) and consultant selection
and employment. The Government made considerable progress indeveloping procurement tools,
particularly with respect to electronic procurement, which facilitate the implementation o f the
basic principles o f transparency, efficiency and economy set forth in the law. However, the
institutional framework i s fragmented and policy oversight limited. This resulted in a
proliferation o f interpretations o f procurement rules and other inefficiencies, and has slowed
down policy reforms and development o f new tools. Among additional tools which should be
developed to increase consistency and efficiency o f implementation are standard bidding
documents for use throughout the public sector. An another important area requiring additional
focus in the ongoing effort to modernize procurement in Brazil i s developing a sustainable
capacity building strategy for public officials carrying out procurement responsibilities with the
objective o f strengthening and professionalizing the function

4.58      Based on this analytical work and the related dialogue between the Bank and the
Government, the conclusion, which is taken into account in deciding the design of the
proposed operation, is that fiduciary risk, including both financial management and
procurement risk, is low and that no additional steps are needed to secure acceptable fiduciary
arrangements for the proposed development policy loan.


                                                 57

Disbursement


4.59         Once the Bank formally notifies the borrower that the loan is available for
withdrawal, the Borrower may submit a withdrawal application so that the proceeds o f the loan
would be deposited by the Bank into an account o f the National Treasury of the Federative
Republic o f Brazil, established at the Central Bank o f Brazil for the Borrower's use.

4.60         The Bank will disburse the single tranche of the loan proceeds into an account of the
Central Bank denominated in USD, which forms part of the country's official foreign
exchange reserves. The Central Bank will immediately credit the disbursed amounts to the
Treasury Single Account, thus becoming available to finance budgeted expenditures. The
National Treasury will then provide the Bank with a written confirmation o f the transaction.


H.        Povertv and Social Impacts 99

4.61         This operation will have positive direct and indirect effects on poverty as discussed
below. The question o f whether the new economic growth program could be expected to have
satisfactory impacts on poverty was detailed in a previous document.Io0 Four main arguments
were developed, namely (i)                the direct effect o f growth on poverty reduction; (ii)                          safeguarding
stability; (iii)protecting social spending program; and, (iv) the quantity and the quality o f
economic growth. Arguments (i) (iv) will be explored indetail below.
                                                and

4.62        Since 1990,poverty levels in Brazil have been reduced while inequality has remained
constant until 2001. Previous research has decomposed poverty changes into variations related
to changes in the income level and to changes in income distribution."' Given Brazil's middle-
income status, there i s a potential to reduce poverty through income redistribution - a given fall
in the poverty rate would cost Brazil a smaller fraction of GDP in redistribution than it would
cost to a poorer country. However, this potential has not been well explored due to the rigid
budgetary spending patterns that left income distribution largely unaltered (See Figures 4.2 and
4.3).

4.63        I t has been acknowledged that, to the extent that these patterns persist, the key to
reduce poverty in Brazil was reigniting growth. It has been recognized that GDP changes have
been the most important factor explaining variations in the poverty rate in Brazil. In the mid-
199Os, stabilization stimulated economic growth. From 1994 to 1997, GDP growth exceeded 3
percent per year. This trend was not sustained and two years o f low growth succeeded: 1997 (0.1
percent) and 1998 (0.8 percent)."* A second surge o f economic growth took place in2000, when
GDP growth reached 4.4 percent. In the following 3 years, however, annual GDP growth rates
hovered around 1.9 percent, due to successive shocks, both domestic, like the energy crisis in
2001 and the presidential elections in 2002, and external, as the September 1lthArgentina's                            and

4.65         I n addition to the two transmission mechanisms through which economic growth
reduces poverty (i.e.,job creation and real wage gains), price stabilization was also associated
with poverty alleviation in Brazil It has been widely recognized that inflation hurts the poor
with a negative relationship between inflation and real per capita earning for all deciles. Inflation
control - established in 1994 with the Plan0 Real - contributed to overall poverty reduction in
Brazil since the mid-l990s.Io5In Brazil, it was found that real wage gains significantly impacted
poverty reduction. For example, real per capita earnings mostly correlated with the minimum
wage are placed in the bottom o f the income distribution, and a one percent real increase in the
minimum wage would increase per capita earnings of the 2nd,107 and 4lh deciles of the income
                                                                                           3rd
distribution by 0.79, 0.5 1 and 0.46 percent, respectively.106,                                  The unemployment elasticity

the income distribution (from -0.56 in the 2nddecile to -0.23 inthe lothor the highest decile), but
(with respect to average income) decreases monotonically as one moves toward the upper tail o f

higher unemployment implies lower per capita earning for all deciles and, thus, higher poverty
levels in overall. In 2004, the number o f jobs created in Brazil was the second highest since
1985, reaching 1.9 million formal jobs (6.3 percent higher than the 2003 figures).''*                                           This
increase was associated with a real raise inthe average earnings per worker o f 1.2 percent.

4.66         Despite current market optimism and Government commitment, macroeconomic
stability and, therefore, poverty reduction in Brazil, still depend onfactors that are not under
control of the authorities. Downturns in the emerging market credit could place the Brazilian
economy under important strain. The fiscal consolidation process in Brazil is still under
implementation and economic growth i s a key variable as far as debt sustainability i s concerned.

4.67         Along with economic growth, better quality of social spendingprograms seems toplay
an important role in poverty reduction. It has been found in Brazil that improvements in social
programs along with economic growth reflected in poverty decreases, since these programs were
politically protected and economically supported by higher growth rates.

4.68         Both education and health indicators in Brazil have been dramatically improving
since the 1990s. Primary education enrollment has become almost universal and infant mortality
rates have nearly halved in most states. In Brazil, the share o f 7 to 14 year-olds in school
increased from 81.O percent to 97.1 percent from 1991 to 2004. However, school quality remains
an issue (one achievement was the introduction o f standardized tests). For example, in 2004,
only 57.6 percent o f primary and secondary teachers o f public school in Brazil had a college
degree.lo9 In addition to qualification o f teachers, challenges also concern the provision of
secondary school enrollment for an increasing number o f students who graduate from the
primary school, many from families without the ability o fpaying for private education. Inhealth,
infant mortality per thousand live births fell from 48 to 27 in the same period, while life
expectancy at birthincrease from 65.6 to 71.7 years. Against a backdrop o f weak income growth,
most o f this progress i s associated with public policies implemented by the Government: in

             n order to alleviate poverty in Brazil, a key step is the reduction of inequality. Brazil

fact that the richest one percent earns the same as the poorest 50 percent. But this highinequality

Brazil are two cash transfer programs created in the previous administration: Bolsa Escola and

4.70       Actions proposed in the Government's growth program since the First Brazilian
Programmatic Loan for Equitable and Sustainable Growth had the pro-poor effects as
predicted. For example, increasing infrastructure access has been found to be one o f the most
pro-poor growth effects inBrazil. Infrastructure remains one o f the four core reforms areas o f the
Second Loan. In addition, access to financial services has also expanded to the poorer social
segments.

4.71       Apart from its direct growth effect, infrastructure improvements have several direct
impacts on poverty reduction. As poorer individuals and underdeveloped areas become
connected to core economic activities, they can access additional productive opportunities. For
example, in poor rural areas, infrastructure expands job opportunities for the less advantaged
people by reducing the costs o f accessing product and factor markets. Infrastructure access can
also raise the value o f the assets o f the poor.'I2 In addition, improving infrastructure services
affects the health and education levels o f the poor. Regarding transportation, sector
improvements facilitate access to healthcare, easy staffing and operation o f clinics, decrease
traffic-related health problems, increase participation in and access to education, promote SME
development, and create jobs.]                 l3 Finally, improving infrastructure services also reduces income
inequality: if each Latin American country raised its infrastructure stock and quality to the levels
of Costa Rica, for example, its Gini coefficient would fall by between 0.02 and 0.10 point.'14

4.72          The Government growth program has specific measures to increase the access of the
poor to financial services. There are four relevant actions: (i)the simplification o f the
procedures to open bank accounts in public banks with the opening o f more than 4.6 million
bank accounts between August 2003 and December 2004, which are exempted o f bank tariffs
and taxes on financial operations; (ii)                    the offering o f loans through payroll deductions, which
increased 89 percent between January and December 2004, reaching RS$ 11.9 billion subjected
to interest rates o f 40.3 percent per year against 70.7 percent per year for other personal credit
lines;"5 (iii)the launching o f the National Program o f Oriented Productive Micro Credit
(PNMPO), aimed at expanding access to productive credit for formal and informal micro-
entrepreneurs with annual revenues up to RS$ 60,000;"6 and (iv) given the rural nature o f
poverty intensity in Brazil, it i s possible to argue that the boost o f credit at special interest rates

Familiar) contributed to poverty reduction in rural areas, increasing from RS$ 2.4 billion in
2002/2003 (904,000 financial operations) to RS$ 4.5 billion in 2003/2004 (1.4 million financial
operations) to RS$ 7.0 billion in 2004/2005."'                          Other actions to encourage lending include new
securitization and insurance mechanisms for the agricultural and housing sectors.

4.73          I n 2004, it became evident the pro-poor nature of economic growth in Brazil,
remarkably was accompanied by a decrease in inequali@. After a period o f very low rate of
decrease, poverty reduction accelerated from 2003 to 2004, with total, rural, urban, and
metropolitan extreme poverty in Brazil falling by 8.0 percent, 6.5 percent, 8.2 percent, and 8.3
percent, respectively. The determinants o f the decrease in extreme poverty in 2004 were the net
growth effect o f 2.8 percent and the decrease in income inequalit re resented by a decrease in
the Gini coefficient from 0.585 in 2003 to 0.573 in 2004.                                             'Ig  The prevalence o f this
distributive effect i s a rare event in the Brazilian social historical series. This phenomenon has
been observed in the country since 2002, when the Gini coefficient was 0.589, but it has been
intensified between 2003 and 2004.'20 With respect to income redistribution, between 2001 and
2004, the income share appropriated by the richest 10 percent decreased from 47.3 percent to
44.7 percent. At the same time, the income share earned by the poorest 50 percent increased
from 12.4 percent to 14.1 percent. Finally, the remaining 40 percent o f the population earned a
larger share o f income, too, and its share increased from 40.0 percent to 41.2 percent.

                                                                       62

I. Environmental,Forests,andOtherNaturalResourceAspects.

4.74    Brazil is probably the developing country with the oldest and most consolidated
environmental licensing system, launched in the early 1970s when industrial growth and the
proliferation o f cars in Rio de Janeiro and Siio Paul0 began to generate significant urban
pollution. Two state environmental agencies (FEEMA and CETESB) equipped and trained
personnel, anticipating actions by the federal Government, which later started to focus on natural
resources problems, such as biodiversity, soil, forests, water, and coastal zone management,
Even today, the state o f Siio Paul0 drives the national pollution management agenda.

4.75     The Government recognizes the need to mainstream environmental management into
its broader economic agenda. Brazil i s an exception among developing countries on
environmental licensing. It has qualified personnel and environmental licensing procedures,
including more complex environmental impact assessments, and standardized and widely
disseminated procedures to seek Government approval. The system includes all states and
municipal Governments are beginningto play a role in environmental licensing. The fact that the
systemis consolidated and disseminated has produced an undesirable rigidity.

4.76     The first loan of the Program had neutral or positive environmental impacts as
expected. It mainly focused on legal, regulatory, institutional, and policy reforms that had no
direct environmental impact. Moreover, the loan supported Brazil's participation in the Clean
Development Mechanism (CDM) and carbon trading under the Kyoto Protocol which has caused
positive environmental impacts. This second loan o f the Program will continue to focus on
policy reforms that are expected to have neutral or positive environmental impacts, as presented
inthis Section.

4.77    Reforms supported under the reduction of               logistics costs section should be
environmentally positive as they should contribute to a decrease in greenhouse emissions by
improving the transport infrastructure (ports, roads and railways). The support to a plan for
the maintenance o f the federal road network will induce a positive action from the Government
which will have to obtain adequate environmental licenses for roads that were built prior to the
establishment o f National Environmental Policy law o f 1981. This action should serve as a
catalyst for a closer relationship between the Ministry o f Environment and the Ministry of
Transport. Moreover, no new roads will be contracted as part o f this loan. Furthermore, by
supporting the restructuring o f the railway concession system, the loan would enable an increase
on usage o f this transportation system which i s more energy efficient than the current system
based on road transport.

4.78     The legal, regulatory, institutional, and policy reforms supported under the objective
of improving the business environment are mainly environmentally neutral. Moreover, the
support to the Lei das Agendas and the institutional framework for PPPs should provide positive
environmental impacts and, in both cases, it should strengthenthe application and monitoring of
the environmental licensing system which should be an integral part o f the concessions. Reforms
aiming at enhancing the efficiency and depth o f the financial sector are also environmentally
neutral as they present no direct relationship with specific investments on the ground (which
could be subject to environmental analysis).




                                                 63

4.79     Reforms supported in the area of innovation are mainly environmentally positive.
Brazil i s now one o f the leading countries benefiting from the C D M mechanism with many
projects ( including the very first one worldwide) with diverse innovate ideas from collecting
greenhouse gases from solid waste dumps to generating energy to producing charcoal (carbon
neutral) to replace coal on smelters. The improved legal and institutional framework regarding
the C D M also enabled the World Bank to invest more through its Carbon Prototype Funds.

4.80     Consistency with the overall environmental policy is achieved by close coordination
with the series of Environmental Sustainability Programmatic loans. The Second Growth Loan
i s negotiated in coordination with the team implementing the First Environmental Loan
(approved in 2004) and its corresponding Technical Assistance Loan (approved one year later).
Therefore, certain environmental licensing elements initially considered for support by the
Growth Program were supported under the environmental program. More importantly, indirect
negative environmental impacts that could be caused by a growth on the business side should be
prevented by a more efficient licensing system that i s being developed in tandem through the
environmental series of programmatic loans.

                                                         Annex 4: Logistics121

Customs

Customs procedures have been improved but they still remain a barrier to trade.                                               Several
clearance procedures have been simplified and/or harmonized with those o f other agencies
involved in trade through several normative instructions issued by SRF over the past two years.
Inparticular, certain export cargoes can now be shipped prior to receiving export clearances, and
clearances for various shipments o f the same shipper can now be consolidated into one process.
Also, the simplified procedures known as the Blue Lane (Linha Azul), which were previously
established for industrial firms with cargoes valued over R$30 million per year, have recently
been expanded to firms with more than R$10 million cargo values, which are expected to
account for almost 70% o f industrial cargo volumes.

In spite of these improvements, the clearance process remains largely inefficient because
customs procedures can only be initiated after (i)the ship is at berth and the cargo (paper)
documentation has been entered to customs, and (ii)                                 all clearances and certifications by other
agencies involved have been completed. Also, cargo inspection ratios remain well above 20%
since effective risk assessment i s not yet part o f the clearance process. And clearances still take
place essentially at the ports because there are still very few inland bonded warehouses and
container depots, given the lack o f flexibility o f the present legislation regulating their
constitution and operation.

The key next steps are therefore: (1) to implement a cargo tracking system (SISCOMEX-
CARGA), which will interface the Merchant Marine ship tracking system (currently under
implementation, see ports section) with SRF's existing clearance system (SISCOMEX) to
automatically provide advance cargo data; (2) to integrate the risk assessment system (RADAR)
with SISCOMEX. The development o f SISCOMEX-CARGA has made little progress in the last
two years because of, inter alia, an insufficient contribution from the Government's data systems
entity (SERPRO), which i s responsible for the project. The design o f the HARPIA system, which
will integrate RADAR and SISCOMEX, has been completed with assistance from two
universities and development i s about to start; and (3) to improve staff management policy,
including evaluation, incentive and training mechanisms.122

In the future, customs clearance processes should proceed in parallel with the processes of the
various agencies involved in ports and airports, but that would involve a substantial re-design o f
SISCOMEX. And draft legislation i s being prepared to revise the legal regime for inland
terminals with a view to facilitate their establishment and operation.

Progress in implementing the decisions o f the MERCOSUL Council to facilitate regional trade
has been slow. Customs clearance procedures continue to be integrated at the border with
Argentina, but they are still beingdiscussed with Paraguay and Uruguay.



I2lPreparedby Aymenc-Albin Meyer.

122Progress on this last point will depend from the conclusion o f the merging between the Federal Revenues and Federal Pension Revenues
Secretaries, as staffpolicies are managed at the Secretary's level and not at the Customs' Department's.



                                                                        81

SRF recently established a trade facilitation division to emphasize trade over revenue collection
objectives. Each year, SRF establishes institutional objectives and operational targets, and
staffing and staff development plans, including for customs clearance. In spite o f the relatively
slow progress on the above-mentioned major reforms needed, SRF's monitoring and evaluation
system shows satisfactory progress in reducing average cargo release times over the past three
years (table 1hereafter).

           Table 1: Average Customs Release Time (in hours, as evaluated by SRF)

                               2002                    2003                   2004
   Imports:
Gross Release time              84.2                   81.4                    79.2
Net Release time                32.1                   24.4                    19.9

  Exports:
Gross Release time              30.9                   21.5                    20.4
Net Release time                30.0                   20.2                    19.6
Source: SRF own data.

Ports

Significant progress was made in the late 1990s and early 2000s in privatizing port terminal
operations and in establishing the new institutional framework, with the local Port Authority
Councils (CAPS) and the Labor Management Organizations (OGMOs), which was outlined in
the Port Reform Law o f 1993. In 2003 the Government established an inter-ministerial working
group to analyze the problems in the sector and to propose an action plan. The working group
prepared recommendations for addressing some o f the main issues, as well as an investment plan
which was approved and issued as the Agenda Portos in2004.

There i s no clear consensus yet on proceeding with the decentralization and/or privatization o f
the port administrations. Only two ports (Itaqui and Santana) have recently been delegated to the
corresponding state or municipality (respectively Maranhao and Macapa, Amapa), bringingthe
total o f delegated ports to twelve. Twenty ports, including Santos and Rio de Janeiro, remain
under federal control through the eight dock companies. Although the dock companies have
been included in the privatization program since 1996, the Government has not initiated, nor i s
preparing to initiate such process. Heavily indebted and faced with numerous judicial actions
linked to labor disputes and with the restrictions resultingfrom their inclusion inthe privatization
program, the dock companies continue to be unable to effectively carry out their new Port
Authority responsibilities. In addition, dock companies are in need o f new staff with manager
profile to reinforce their capacity to operate as port authorities. A first hiring program i s being
implemented, which would benefit the 4 main public ports.

Within such policy framework which excludes broad delegation and major privatizations, the
Government may consider privatizing a few selected secondary ports with adequate operational
conditions (such as Sao Sebastiao, Sao Francisco do Sul, etc.) which could effectively compete
with major public ports and contribute to improve the efficiency o f the ports system as a whole.




                                                 82

In regulating port services, some progress was made with the issuance by ANTAQ of a norm
which specifies procedures and provides guidelines to port administrations for the leasingo f port
facilities and areas to private operators and for regulating and supervising such leases. ANTAQ
i s also proceeding with the establishment o f a ports statistics system, now operational in 19 ports,
which will allow for monitoring and evaluating the performance o f individual ports and o f the
entire system.

Inorder to coordinate the implementationofthe International Ship and Port Facility (ISPS) Code
agreed within the IMO, the Government established an inter-ministerial group in early 2003.
The National Commission for Public Safety in Ports (CONPORTOS) issued a number o f
resolutions requiring each port to carry out a safety risk analysis and to prepare a safety plan for
controlling port perimeters and accesses for employees, vehicles and ships. Special budgets have
been allocated to ports (R$ 60 million) and the police (R$ 40 million) for this purpose. Progress
was made in implementing these measures in the major ports, particularly Santos, which i s
expected to be certified shortly by CONPORTOS.

The labor issue, including over-dimensioned gang sizes (and excessive, registered, for-hire work
force) and excessive workers' compensations, which substantially impact port costs, has not yet
been fully resolved.      The pool o f for-hire stevedores i s now estimated at about 27,000
nationwide, down from about 35,000 in 2002. This reduction, together with the substantial
increase in port traffic, has alleviated the problem countrywide, and somewhat resolved it in a
few ports such as Vitoria, Rio Grande, and Salvador, where operators and labor unions have
agreed to adjust labor hiring to actual requirements. But for-hire labor costs continue to be a
problem in the major ports, particularly Rio de Janeiro and Santos. A key next step therefore
remains the negotiation o f some form o f collective agreement between terminal operators and
labor unions, facilitated by the Government, possibly within the forum o f the Camara Setorial
Portuaria or a new national commission for port development proposed by the Labor Ministry.

Regarding the improvement o f electronic data interchange (EDI) in the ports system, the inter-
ministerial working group has recommended the establishment o f a special commission to foster
and coordinate efforts from the various entities concerned, and proposed a draft decree for this
purpose. Only limited progress was made on the ground, in computerizing the Merchant Marine
ship tracking system, while the Customs' SISCOMEX-CARGA project remains idle. A key next
step i s therefore the approval o f the draft decree establishing the proposed commission.

The Ministry o f the Environment i s promoting environmental management in ports and the
protection o f coastal areas through three main programs: the Port and Environment Agenda, the
Integrated Coastal Environmental Management Project, and the Maritime Environment Agenda.
Progress was made recently under the former agenda in preparing a National Program for
Environmental Training o f Port Staff and in offering three courses for port managers and
professionals. Environmental management i s also being strengthened, under this program, in
twelve priority ports, through improved procedures and training o f management and technical
staff.

The Agenda Portos identifies the critical bottlenecks in the ports system, and defines key
investment priorities in 11 major ports. The private sector has been investing heavily interminal



                                                   83

facilities and equipment in the face o f the rapidly expanding external and domestic coastal
trades. But progress has been slow in undertaking the major public investments, which involve
capital and maintenance dredging works in port access channels, due to slow environmental
clearance processes and to the limited capacity o f the heavily-regulated dredging industry.

Roads

The condition o f the road network remains significantly deteriorated, with still about 25% o f the
network only in good condition and an estimated 37% in poor condition (with an IRI above 5.0,
see graph below). But the Government remains committed to carry out the necessary actions
described below to increase the portion o f the road network in good condition to 50% and to
decrease road transport costs by 5% in about 4 years.

There i s now a broad consensus in the federal and state Governments that highways o f mainly
local interest (about 15,000 km) should be transferred to state jurisdictions. But the protracted
negotiations between the states and the federation on the conditions for such transfers have not
yet been successfully concluded, most states still seeking that these roads be rehabilitated to
satisfactory condition prior to their transfer, in spite o f their earlier acceptance against cash
transfers (MP82, December 2002). And because o f a lack o f interest o f the federal level to
rehabilitate such roads, there i s also increasing interest in many states to assume responsibility
for administering the remaining interstate federal highways, provided that the corresponding
financial  resources are also transferred. Both sides are still working on draft legislation to
proceed with the transfer program initiated inthe late 1990sand to reclassify the network (SNV),
two key steps for decentralizing the administration o f the highway network. But prospects for
reaching a consensus are still unclear at this stage.

Although there has not been any new highway concession in the recent past, the Government,
with technical support from ANTT, updated the feasibility studies and carried out a
comprehensive review o f the bidding and contract documents for a second phase o f the
concession program consisting o f eight segments totaling about 2,500 km. These documents are
currently being finalized to incorporate the comments made by the Tribunal das Contas da
Uniao (TCU). Key next steps will be: (i) proceed with the biddingand contractingprocess for
                                            to
these eight new (second phase) concessions; and (ii)   to contract out the studies for a third phase.
Also, the Government has selected three highways as pilot candidates for public-private
partnerships (PPP) in accordance with the legislation which was recently approved by the
congress. The Government has contracted IFC to undertake the pre-investment studies for one o f
these highways. Key next steps are to contract out the studies for the other two selected pilot
highways.     The PPP legislation opened the possibility o f transferring highways requiring
substantial investments to private operators while keeping toll rates acceptable to road users
(through some form o f public sector participation). This, provided that Brazil's fiscal situation
and investment rating continue to improve, should allow the 10,000 km medium term target for
concessions to be substantially completed.


Rehabilitation works and maintenance services have been contracted through long-term, output-
based contracts has increased from 15% to about 22% o f the non-concessioned, non-transferable
network, with the contractors responsible for achieving specified levels o f service.           Good


                                                  84

progress has been made at the technical level to improve the federal road rehabilitation and
maintenance program's efficiency: (a) the federal road rehabilitation and maintenance partly i s
included in the Government's Pluri-Annual Investment Program, which guarantees that given
budgets be fully made available; and (b) DNIT has defined a new maintenance policy, based on
an improved catalogue o f technical solutions, standard bidding document, supervision
procedures and an integrated program monitoring system. Taken the above into account, the
Program's target o f 30% couldbe exceeded inthe short-term.

But progress at the technical level needs to be complemented by improved staffing,
administrative and managerial capacity in DNIT as a whole, in order for the reform's objective
of strengthening highway management capacity to come close to be achieved. Some progress
was made in approving a new staffing and compensation plan (plano de cargos e salarios) for
DNIT, which provides for salary levels more compatible with present market levels, and allows
the recruitment o f new staff. But DNIT i s not yet structured to effectively undertake its
administrative, financial, audit and overall monitoring and evaluation functions. The key next
steps will be to modernize and integrate DNIT's information systems, strengthen its internal
audit capacity with experienced auditors, and structure a training program for newly-hired staff.

MultimodalTransport

Substantial progress has been made in establishing the conditions for the development of
efficient multimodal transport and logistics options.

The operational and ownership restructuring o f the railway concessions, initiated by ANTT in
2003, has now been completed. Several lines which were part of, and had been privatized
together with the ex-FEPASA (Sa0 Paulo) railway, have been incorporated into the networks
operated by FCA, ALL and Novoeste, respectively, improving access o f these railroads to Sao
Paulo and/or Santos. ANTT enacted and i s already enforcing new regulations for joint and
interchange railway traffic and track rights, and for captive or railway-dependant shippers, which
have already improved railroad operations, particularly in the Sao Paulo - Santos region.
Regulations have also been issued for licensing Multimodal Transport Operators (MTOs). At
this stage, 146 MTOs have been licensed and progress was made in resolving insurance and
taxation issues. All these actions are increasing the competitiveness o f multimodal alternatives
to door-to-door road transport.

The restructuringo f the federal transport administration has proceeded, although at a slow pace.
ANTT has made substantial progress in developing its strategic planning and operational
functions, and in recruiting and training staff; it i s now in the process o f hiring350 new staff to
establish five regional offices which will strengthen its capacity for supervisingrailway, highway
and interstate bus concessions. The Transport Ministry (MT) has consolidated its planning
duties under a unique secretariat, which now works on integrated development strategies rather
than on sub-sector, isolated projects. The planning department undertook to prepare a national
transport and logistics plan to identify critical infrastructure improvements designed to resolve
connectivity bottlenecks, and to provide incentives for a redistribution o f freight away from
trucking to more efficient multimodal options. A key next step i s to strengthen MT's planning
department through recruitment o f new, experienced staff and training o f the existing staff,



                                                  85

With the improved legal and institutional framework for public-private partnerships (PPP)
established through the recent legislation and the establishment o f the PPP unit inMPOG and o f
related inter-ministerial committee and working group, five transport projects were selected as
PPP candidates for further pre-investment studies. These include the previously-mentioned three
highways, the North-South railway project, and the Sao Paul0 ring railway (Ferroanel). Key
next steps will be to contract out feasibility studies for structuring financings for the two railway
projects. Regarding the Ferroanel, the federal and the Sao Paul0 state Governments still need to
reach agreement on the terms o f reference and on the financing and supervision arrangements for
such study. In the medium, a pipeline o f several PPP transport projects would have been
developed.

As part o f the Government's efforts, coordinated by MPOGISPI, for establishing a
comprehensive system for monitoring the implementation and for evaluating the results o f public
expenditure programs (as a basis for carrying out the annual reviews o f the PPA), MT has carried
out a diagnostic of the existing systems in the Ministry, and particularly in DNIT. A key next
step i s to prepare terms o f reference and to contract out services for designing and implementing
such systems.

   Annex 5: The Stateof BankruptcyCases under New Law, CentralCourts of SGo Pau10'*~

The following i s based on two lengthy interviews in SZo Paulo and additional documents and
statistics provided by those interviewed. Interviewees were Judge Alexandro Lazzarini o f the
first vara de falCncias e recuperagiio judicial in central SZo Paulo and Sidnei Benetti, president o f
the special Camara for falCncias e recuperagiio judicial.

First a word on structure. In SZo Paulo's central court district, it was decided, at the instigation
of Benetti and others, to set up two specialized varas for first instance cases. These courts will
receive all new filings, as well as cases already being processed (under the old law) by other
judges in the central district. In the rest of the state, bankruptcy cases will continue to be heard
by ordinary civil judges. All appeals (of existing and new cases) will now be seen by a
specialized chamber. There were several reasons for both decisions: first, it was believed that
specialized judges could deal with the cases more rapidly, taking advantage o f their greater
familiarity with the topic, and second, the creation o f specialized courts was believed to
guarantee more consistency inrulings. Third, the single chamber may be especially important in
discouraging appeals - the lottery effect ("some desembargador will rule in my favor'') i s now
gone, and with it, much of the incentive for the appeal.

Aside fi-om this structural change in Siio Pau10,'~~               the law is believed to be an improvement in
several senses. A minimum value for pedidos de falencia (creditors' request that an entity be
processed for bankruptcy) will eliminate some o f the nuisance cases (filed for very small
amounts, often to pressure a debtor to pay or just to make trouble). However, the floor i s still
low (40 minimum salaries or roughly Reais 12,000).                          The introduction o f the recuperaggo
judicial (RJ) whereby the affected enterprise requests a restructuring o f debt i s also believed to
be superior to the auto-falencia, which was never used much in any case. One change made to
the draft law was the addition o f provisions to allow the sale o f seized assets before the workout
with the entire list o f creditors. This was thought necessary because in the past, the lengthy
workouts often meant that assets lost value. Whether the other new rules will speed up the work
out and whether the state as priority creditor will leave anything for the rest remains to be seen.
Bothjudges believedthat the test cases will be the big RJs now underway - Varig, Parmelat, and
Kwickaser.

Judge Lazarrini provided statistics on the new filings in his court, which he estimates are
comparable to those o f the one other vara serving S5o Paulo's central district. The figures are as
follows for the months June to November (with both June and November representing partial
periods) and include cases transferred from other varas as well as new filings (although Iwas
given abreakdown only for the RJs).


     0    Pedidos de Falencia - 376
     0    FalCncias- 11 (these are all transferred cases corresponding to falhcias decretadas under
          the old rules)
     0    RecuperagZoJudicial -20 (of these only 9 are new filings)

During this same period, 90 falCncias were decreed (Le. the process begun) and 6 were closed.
As in the past, the majority of these are the result of pedidos de falCnica. However, Lazarrini
noted that most o f these never produce satisfactory results - the affected company often has
disappeared, has no assets, or otherwise leaves nothing for the creditors to collect. Presumably,
in the cases where the creditor's motive is to force a payment from a solvent company (which
could also be done through an aqiio de execuqiio, but without the added pressure on the creditor -
inability to take out other loans, etc), the creditor may pay up to avoid the negative consequences
before or soon after thejudge accepts the action.

Lacking statistics from the period before the law went into effect, it i s impossible to say whether
the situation has changed. The oddity o f Brazil i s the relatively greater use o f the process by
individual creditors and the relatively lesser use by the companies themselves, a profile likely to
be modified (because o f the new limits on the amounts for which a PF can be filed) but not
reversed by the new law. This pattern has led, at least inJudge Lazarrini's experience, to another
oddity - the use o f individual lawyers to handle the workout process even in the larger
recuperaqaes judiciais. His reason i s the following: as these lawyers work on the pedidos de
falencia, which most often produce no results, they tend to receive no payment for their services.
Hence he believed it was fairer to give the work on the recuperaq6es to them as well, a process in
which they receive ajudicially determined monthly fee (for them and their team) which will later
be deducted from the 5 percent o f the workout value to which they will be entitled. This practice
was apparently used in the past and so far has not been altered. The question o f course i s how
they will do in the more complex proceedings under the new law and whether the alternative
candidates (the big accounting and management firms) will accept this outcome.

Both the interviewees and the authors contributing to a special issue o f the Advogado devoted to
the new law anticipate the possible need for further adjustments over time. The hope o fcourse is
that the recuperaqiio judicial will both be used to a greater extent and that it will serve the
purpose o f preserving companies facing temporary insolvency but with a chance o f longer term
survival. Over time, this new addition should take a larger share o f the varas' time, with the
pedidos de falCncia and the falCncias decretadas decreasing inimportance. Among specialists in
the area there i s considerable enthusiasm about the new law, but all admit that the improvements
face a steep learning curve among all parties as the underlyingphilosophy i s quite different, as
are the practices introduced.

                          Annex 6: Simplification of Business Entry and Operation'25

Introduction

Facilitation o f entry and exit o f firms into business i s widely recognized as a key determinant o f
productivity and thus o f long term growth.'26 Barriers to entry reduce productivit directly: new
firms have been found to exhibit both higher and faster growing productivity.12YHighstart-up
costs also inhibit entry and investment by making it less likely that new firms become formal, a
problem particularly serious inBrazil, where the level o f informality i s considered high.

The promotion o f institutional changes in order to remove barriers to do business involves thus
addressing the time spent and the administrative barriers to the entry and exit o f firms into
operation. In Brazil, time costs seem to be the main administrative problem for firms. The
country does not have excessive pecuniary costs o f firm registry; nor does the number o f
procedures to register appear a major concern, although 15 procedures in Brazil is still higher
than Korea (12), Chile             (lo),  and Mexico (7).12* The time it takes to register a new firm in Brazil
i s substantially longer than in some o f its main regional and international competitors.

Data from "Doing Business, 2004" reveals that it can take up to 152 days to start a business in
Brazil (if the firm is located in Sao Pau10)'~~compared with 58 days in Mexico and only 27 days
inChile. The comparison is starker ifwe include some o f the more important OECD countries.
Brazil i s significantly higher than comparators such as Mexico, Korea or Chile which approach
the OECD average o f just over 30 days. In the most innovative countries, such as Ireland,
Australia, and the US, time to register a company is often below ten days.'30

The lack of unification between Federal, State and Municipal registration processes i s one main
cause o f de1a~s.I~'For example, a firm must register with federal, state and municipal tax
registries: about 25 days on average. According to the Doing Business database, the bulk o f time
to register i s taken at the municipal level: 120 o f the 158 days (76 percent). There i s also great
variation between municipal (and between state) administrations. Data suggest local discretion to
ration entry, whether inpursuit o f rents or simply to comply with outdated norms.

There are several permits and licenses requested at the state and municipal level. These range
from municipal health and fire inspections to hurdles to acquiring and developing land. These

requirements can remove the incentive to register a business formally. This may lead to a vicious
circle o f informality, which erodes the tax base and Government ability to provide public goods,
fiu-ther reducing the attraction o f operating formally.

Data from the Brazil Investment Climate Assessment (ICA) show that state registration and
permits took the longest time to obtain. Brazilian firms that registered within the last two years
(new firms) reported that it took the longest time to obtain registration from the State
Environmental Registration (FEEMA), 83 days, followed by the Federal Environment
Registration (IBAMA) and the Central Bank Registration for foreign investors, 46 days.
Obtaining a permit from Junta Comercial and the Secretaria de Receita Federal took 29-30 days.
With respect to tax registration, registration with the State Tax Authority took 26 days compared
to 20 days to register with the Municipal Tax Authority. An inscription in the National Institute
of Social Security (INSS) took 25 days and to register a new firm inthe Notary took 22 days, the
same number o f days for a Health Inspection.

Prior actions

There are several initiatives being carried out in Brazil with the aim o f reducing the time spent
on starting a business. The publication o f the Doing Business report in 2004, showing that it
could take up to 152 days to open a firm in Brazil triggered a series o f initiatives, both at the sub
national and the federal levels. The federal Government created a working group headed by casa
Civil to examine this issue. Specific measures were adopted in Sao Paulo, as well as in several
states of the Northeast. The Senate recently created a group to examine the issue.

Among the main actions taken to date there are: (a) the establishment o f the Simples tax
registration system for SMEs; (b) the extension o f the legislation to the so-called Supersimples
law currently in the legislature; (c) elements o f the tax reform that will simplify the
administrative burden on firms o f cascading taxes such as the ICMS, and PIS/PASEP system,
and (d) simplification o f the procedures for environmental licensing.

Regarding the obstacles to close a business in Brazil, the recent approved Bankruptcy Law
represents a major step, as the time spent in the bankruptcy process i s expected to be
significantly reduced within the new framework.

OnOctober 27`h, 2005, the House o f Representatives approved the Provisory Measure MP255/05 kwon as
the new "MP do Bern." It i s composed by 134 articles related to welfare and fiscal issues inBrazil and
should be effective starting on January Ist, 2006. This piece o f legislation provides both general and
specific benefits.

tax revenues o f R$ 5 billionper year.

Objectivesof the program

The objective o f this component i s to increase competition by reducing administrative costs to
businesses. It aims at doing so by simplifying procedures for business registration, in order to
reduce the time spent inthis process, recognized as being too high.

The main future challenge lies inachieving a simplification o f administrative procedures such as
company registration and related procedures across federal, state, and municipal authorities. To
complement these changes, the Federal Government i s initiating reforms with key states and
municipalities to simplify procedures inkey areas.

There have been some attempts to reduce the time needed to register a company, for example the
"Sistema Facil" in a few selected states, but they have yet to be assessed rigorously. Such an
analysis, particularly over a few years and across states, would determine whether such efforts
significantly reduce administrative barriers and allow for more efficient implementation across
states and municipalities.

The program

The federal administration i s currently developing two different projects that are related to
business simplification. The first one i s an integration o f tax administration at the three levels o f
Government, which will also include other agencies involved in the process. The second



                                                  91

initiative i s a project o f law, still not sent to Congress, which recreates the FACIL system and
proposes some measures to simplify the business registrationprocess.

The project on integration o f the revenues services at the three levels o f Government i s underway
and i s thus the one that will be completed in the short run. Although not mandatory, it i s backed
by a constitutional amendment (EC 42, on tax reform) that establishes that Governments should
pursue the integration o f their revenues services.'32Moreover, the project i s not restricted to the
revenue service - vertical integration - , but encompasses all other agencies involved in the
process 6f creation o f a firm, thus addressing the issue o f horizontal integration.

The process i s under way, as several workshops have been already held involving Secretaria da
Receita Federal (federal revenues service) and the state and municipal revenue services. An
agreement was signed involving 19 states (out o f 27) and 8 m~nicipalities.'~~Definitions are
expected to be finalized and the single roster to be ready in June 2006 and operational a few
months later.

Expectedimpactand indicators

Significant gains interms o f time spent in the registration o f business are expected to arise from
the adoption o f the synchronization o f the tax collection system - as previously mentioned this
project is not restricted to the tax collection process itself, and will encompass other agencies
involved inthe process o fbusiness registry.

One o f the reasons for the excessive length o f time taken to open a business is the sequencing o f
the process, involving registeringdocuments in different agencies o f the 3 levels o f Government,
and the looping process frequently associated to it. It i s not unusual to see entrepreneurs
interested inopening a business having to restart the whole process after missingsome deadlines.

The second important channel through it the current initiative can produce an impact in the time
spent for business registration i s the synchronization itself and the intensive use o f information
technology that will take place. The process o f codification will be done once and for all, the
process o f consultation will be registered and will be accessedby the several agencies involved,
reducing the time spent in subsequent phases.

This measure can therefore bringa significant albeit moderate progress in terms of time spent to
open a business, through the effects of synchronization and elimination o f the necessity o f the
work to be redone as it often happens currently.

The natural indicator i s therefore the time spent in the process o f opening a business. In pilot
municipalities, a main indicator for reduction in time o f procedures should be targeted, such as

Proceduresto open a business inBrazil

The following legal steps to opening a business in Brazil refer to limited liability partnerships,
the most common business type inthe country:


    0   Registration o f the partnership contract at the State Commercial Registry (Junta
Comercial): it lasts five days and costs RS$ 59.06. This step aims at verifying the authenticity o f
the signatures o f the partnership contract. Partners have to bring a copy o f the contract along
with authentication o f a public notary. After processing and approving the request, the
application process i s completed and i t i s assigned a registry number (NIRE) to the partnership.
    0   Registration o f Corporate Taxpayers (CNPJ) at the Federal Revenue Services (Receita
Federal): it costs RS$ 10.00, lastingbetween five and seven days. Since Apri1/2001, this process
has to be done on-line. Ifthe application has no errors, some documents have to be sent either by
mail or bybusiness associations' couriers to the Federal Revenue Service.
    0   Registration with the State Revenue Services (Receita Estadual): i t i s free, lasting
between 17 and 23 days. The partnership has to fill an on-line request to register with the state
value-added tax on services and circulation o f goods (ICMS) corporate taxpayers' registry. After
getting clearance from the State Revenue Services, the business partners have to show proof o f
partnership registration within the Junta Comercial, CNPJ registration and business address,
among others, in addition to personal identification. If no errors are found, the application i s
approved and its number i s provided on-line. After finishing this process, the business partners
have to request an "Authorization to Print Fiscal Documents" (AIDF) within the State Revenue
Services - this request is free, can also be done on-line and lasts, on average, five days. After
getting the AIDF, fiscal documents have to be printed by a graphic firm authorized by the State
Revenue Services.
    0   Obtaining the "Reference Working Terms" (Termo de Consulta de Funcionamento) with
the City Hall: it i s free and lasts around 15 days. In order to obtain this certificate, several
documents must be provided by the business partners, including personal identification and a
copy o f the municipal property tax receipt associated with the real state property to which the
certificate refers to. At the same time, it can be requested a business registration within the
Securities Contribution Registry (Cadastro de Contribuintes Mobilicirios), which should indicate
the main business activity to be developed by the partnership, its location and other information
related to the business identification.
    0   Business Working Permit from the Citv Hall: ifthe business real state property will have
up to 100 workers in its physical location, the document issued by the City Hall is named Auto
de LicenCa de Funcionamento, taking around 30 days to be ready. Several documents have to be
provided within the application for this permit, including a copy o f real state property ownership,
a copy o f the registered CNPJ, copy o f environmental permits if the activity threats the
environment, a copy the registration with the Securities Contribution Registry, and proof o f fire
security systems installed at the business property. If it will have more than 100 workers, the
document i s called Alvara de Funcionamento - the provisory document takes five days to be
ready and the final certificate i s issued within 180 days after its request with the City Hall.

                                               Annex 7: The Financial Sector'34

The Legal and Institutional Infrastructure for Financial Deepening

Modernizingpayment systems and strengthening the oversight role of the Central Bank

In May 2003, the amendment o f Article 192 of the Constitution removed a major legal
impediment for financial sector reform in Brazil. The requirement that the financial system be
governed by a single overarching law was lifted, thus allowing the development o f specialized
legislation tackling various issues on the agenda. A number o f fundamental legislative proposals
for financial sector reform have been under preparation for some time, and their presentation to
Congress awaited the amendment o f Article 192. This includes draft new legislation to provide a
legal underpinning for the autonomy o f monetary policy in Brazil. Also under preparation for a
significant period has been a revised law on bank failure resolution, which would extend to the
banking sector the bankruptcy legislation for corporate insolvencies approved in December
2004.135The urgency o f this reform has become clear lately, given the inadequacy o f the existing
legal framework in resolving the recent failure o f a medium-sized private bank in Brazil.
Meanwhile, proposed amendments to the statutes o f the FGC, (Fundo Garantidor de Creditos, the
deposit insurance fund administrator), which would expand its role inbank failure resolution and
also broaden its financing options and give more responsibility to management have also been
approved.136

Capitalizing on the progress made during the previous operation, the Government has shown
continued commitment to the objectives of passing sound fundamental legislation and enhancing
systemic risk control. In fact, most of the key targets identified by the previous loan as next steps
inthis areahavebeenlargely exceeded.

A number o f other initiatives have been taken over the last few years to strengthen the oversight
function o f the Central Bank over payment systems. Inthe first quarter o f 2004, an international
auditing firm has advised the Central Bank on setting up procedures to manage operational risks
within the large value payment system, including its role in reserve management. Over the last
few years, the Central Bank has made significant progress in minimizing risks in the payment
systems by setting strict eligibility requirements for counterparties, performing regular on-site
inspections including stress tests, monitoring peak transaction volumes and providing payment
guarantees. Additionally, steps have been taken to strengthen and clarify the oversight role o f the
Central Bank in the risk management at clearing houses. A number o f contingency measures
have been put in place to minimize operational risks. Furthermore, the BCB is constantly
involved inthe supervision o f risk management mechanisms in the securities settlement systems
at the Bolsa de Mercaderias e Futuros (BM&F). Since the beginning o f 2003, the BCB has also
been reporting regularly on payment system issues in the new Financial Stability Report
(Relatorio de Estabilidade Financiera). The report presents a chapter on payment systems


   Preparedby Marco Sorge and Eduardo Urdapilleta.

   Among other things, the new corporate bankruptcy law has introduced the transfer o f creditor rights as a new legal instrument inthe resolution
of failed corporations. This is expectedto reducerisks for banks and boost lending.
"`Resolution  3024 o f theCMN of October 24,2002,



                                                                      96

together with other sessions on macroeconomic issues, banking supervision and systemic risk.
Recent issues have extensively addressed some important aspects o f the SPB such as the reform
of the large value systems, the project for reform o f retail payment systems and a test o f risk
management procedures at several clearinghouses.

Reforms in the legal infrastructure have been paralleled by significant improvements in the
financial infrastructure and in particular in Brazil's payment systems. The Brazilian Real Time
Gross Settlement System (Sistema de Transferencia de Reservas, STR) was launched
successfully in April 2002. The personnel o f the Banco Central do B r a d (BCB) have acquired
substantial knowledge on RTGS systems design and implementation throughout the world and
have achieved an appropriate balance between risk mitigation and system efficiency in the
designo f the STR. While the volume o f operations on the STR has grown very rapidly inrecent
years, its technological platform has been upgraded and residual risk in the STR and the SELIC
systems (Government securities settlement) have been audited. Both the technological platform
and the mathematical models used for management o f systemic liquidity have been upgraded.

While the technological platform for large-value transactions is fully installed and operational,
following international best practices, there i s considerable room for improvement in the
efficiency  o f retail payment systems and instruments. Inefficiencies in retail payment systems
infrastructure include the low level o f interoperability between banks and clearinghouses, among
Automatic Teller Machine (ATM) and Point o f Sale (POS) networks and the lack o f
standardization in systems communication protocols. In Brazil, there are several national ATM
networks which are not interconnected, customers o f one bank cannot access other bank's
network, posing an infrastructurebarrier to competition. Similarly, the infrastructure for clearing
and settling transactions among banks i s very fragmented. These obstacles prevent all
participants, direct and indirect, from benefiting from scale economies and impose a sizable
economic cost to the Brazilian society. Regardingpayment instruments, the predominant use o f
cash and checks implies high transportation and processing costs and higher exposure to fraud
and counterfeiting. The BCB is currently working on what has been called SPB-2 (Sistema de
Pagamento Brasileiro-2), a second generation reform aiming at the modernization o f retail
payment instruments, in order to promote cheaper and more efficient substitutes for checks and
cash itself. As an important step in the effort o f rationalizing retail payment systems in Brazil,
the Central Bank has recently issued an official report containing a diagnostics of the current
inefficiencies and a blueprint for reform. This had been identified as a key next step supported by
the previous operation. The main objectives o f SPB-2 are to integrate ATM networks,
standardize communication protocols and promote more intensive use o f electronic means o f
payment. In designing this reform agenda, the Department o f Banking Operations and Payment
Systems at the BCB has benefited        also from contacts with several other central banks, in
particular inEurope and in Latin America.

Looking forward, the next steps supported by this loan in the modernization o f payment systems
include: i)the full implementation o f the SPB-2 project for retail payments and ii)rationalizing
the infrastructure of interbank money markets and o f security exchanges. Both objectives appear
of paramount importance for financial sector deepening in Brazil. The increased efficiency of
retail payment systems, including a better interconnection among ATM networks and a
significant increase inthe use o f credit cards, will be among the key outcome indicators.



                                                  97

A New Anti-Trust Regime in the Banking Sector

Highintermediation spreads and the significant concentration in Brazil's banking industry have
led many to worry about the degree o f competition in the banking sector. Concentration has
increased since the mid-l990s, following a number o f closures, mergers and acquisitions. It i s
estimated that about 70 percent o f all short-term bank deposits are held by Brazil's five largest
banks 137

These outcomes inpart reflected a lack o f legislation in this area, which only this year has begun
to be successfully resolved. Up until last year, there was no clear division o f responsibilities
between the Central Bank and the Anti-trust authorities (CADE). Inprinciple, the Central Bank
was responsible for the oversight o f mergers and acquisitions as well as market conduct issues in
the banking sector both for operations with systemic importance and for smaller ones.'38The role
o f the Anti-trust authorities was limited to other sectors. While inconsistent case law had
contributed to blur this division o f responsibilities in the past,'39 the Central Bank's exclusive
authority to approve all merger and acquisitions o f financial institutions inBrazil was confirmed
inahighlevel legalopinion in2001.*40

However, the effectiveness o f competition and anti-trust oversight in the banking sector had
remained quite limited in practice. This i s because the Central Bank analyzed bank mergers from
the perspective of financial system stability, rather than that o f consumer protection. Almost
automatic approval was granted, as long as the bank holding company was in good health,
minimum capital requirements were met and the bank participated in the national deposit
insurance system.141

To address these shortcomings, a new legal bill was jointly presented to Congress by the Central
Bank and CADE in November 2002, which proposed a formal division of responsibilities
between the Central Bank and anti-trust authorities. The Central Bank's responsibility would be
limitedto systemic issues which affect the "good functioning" o f the banking sector, whereas all
other competition issues were to be transferred to anti-trust a~th0rities.I~~The proposed bill has
not yet gained parliamentary approval. However, a formal agreement has recently been reached

antitrust regime for the banking industry, along the lines o f the proposed Banking Competition
Law. This formal agreement has been published in the Diario Oficial da Uniao on the 15th of
